<EFX_CONTROL_AND_PROCEDURES>
<A NAME="FIS_CONTROL_AND_PROCEDURES"></A>
<P ALIGN="CENTER" STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:CENTER;">
<B>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	CONTROLS AND PROCEDURES
</FONT>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Disclosure Controls and Procedures
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-INDENT:1.0IN;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The United States Securities and Exchange Commission (the &#147;Commission&#148;) defines &#147;disclosure controls and procedures&#148;&nbsp;as controls and other procedures of an issuer that are designed to ensure that information required to be disclosed by an issuer in the reports that it files or submits under the Exchange Act is recorded, processed, summarized and reported, within the time periods specified in the Commission&#146;s rules&nbsp;and forms.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-INDENT:.5IN;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	After evaluating the effectiveness of Canadian National Railway Company&#146;s disclosure controls and procedures as of the end of the fiscal year covered by this report, Canadian National Railway Company&#146;s President and Chief Executive Officer (the &#147;CEO&#148;) and its Executive Vice President and Chief Financial Officer (the &#147;CFO&#148;) have concluded that Canadian National Railway Company&#146;s disclosure controls and procedures were effective as of the end of the fiscal year covered by this report.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Management&#146;s Annual Report on Internal Control over Financial Reporting
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-INDENT:.5IN;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The report of management on our internal control over financial reporting is located under the heading &#147;Management&#146;s Report on Internal Control Over Financial Reporting&#148; in our audited consolidated financial statements, which are filed as Exhibit&nbsp;99.2 to this annual report on Form&nbsp;40-F, and is incorporated by reference herein.
</FONT>
</P>
</EFX_CONTROL_AND_PROCEDURES>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-INDENT:.5IN;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="TIMES NEW ROMAN" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Registrant&#146;s board of directors has reviewed the Registrant&#146;s corporate governance practices in response to the U.S. Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002, applicable rules&nbsp;of the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission, as well as the NYSE Corporate Governance Standards (the &#147;NYSE Standards&#148;). Except as disclosed on its website, the Registrant&#146;s corporate governance practices do not differ significantly from that followed by U.S. domestic companies under the NYSE Standards. A discussion of differences is available at the Registrant&#146;s Internet website, www.cn.ca under the caption &#147;Delivering Responsibly / Governance&#148;.

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	CN was incorporated in 1919 by special act of the Parliament of Canada with the appointment of its first Board of Directors by Order in Council in 1922.&#160; CN&#146;s continuance under the
<I>
	Canada Business Corporations Act
</I>
	was authorized by the
<I>
	CN Commercialization Act
</I>
	and was effected by Certificate of Continuance dated August&nbsp;24, 1995.&#160; On November&nbsp;9, 1995, CN filed Articles of Amendment in order to subdivide its outstanding common shares (Common Shares).&#160; As of November&nbsp;28, 1995, CN ceased to be a Crown corporation and became a publicly held corporation with its Common Shares listed on the New York Stock Exchange (NYSE) and the Toronto Stock Exchange (TSX).&#160; On April&nbsp;19, 2002, CN filed Articles of Amendment in order to provide that shareholder meetings may be held at certain specified places in the U.S. Such constating documents are hereinafter collectively referred to as the Articles.
</FONT>
</P>

<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	CN&#146;s goal is to deliver valuable transportation services for its customers and to grow the business at low incremental cost. A clear strategic agenda, driven by a commitment to innovation, productivity, supply-chain collaboration, running trains safely, and minimizing environmental impact, drive the Company&#146;s efforts to create value for

	&nbsp;

</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	customers. CN thereby creates value for its shareholders by striving for sustainable financial performance through profitable top-line growth, adequate free cash flow and return on invested capital. CN is also focused on returning value to shareholders through dividend payments and share repurchase programs.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The initiatives undertaken by CN in the last three years to achieve its growth and profitability goals and to enhance shareholder value can be grouped into a few key areas.&#160; These include acquisitions and dispositions, targeted capital investment spending and other initiatives to strengthen the Company&#146;s position in the marketplace, as well as financial management initiatives, as described below.
</FONT>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">

	6
</FONT>
</B>
<B>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	Highlights
</FONT>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;PUNCTUATION-WRAP:SIMPLE;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Leadership Changes
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;PUNCTUATION-WRAP:SIMPLE;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On June&nbsp;7, 2016, CN announced a number of leadership changes including Claude Mongeau&#146;s decision, due to a health condition, to step down from his role as President and Chief Executive Officer (CEO) and member of the Board of Directors at the end of June&nbsp;2016, as well as the appointment of Executive Vice-President and Chief Financial Officer (CFO) Luc Jobin to President and CEO on July&nbsp;1, 2016 and a member of the Board of Directors on June&nbsp;30, 2016. Additionally, on June&nbsp;27, 2016, the Company announced that Ghislain Houle would become Executive Vice-President and CFO, and that Mike Cory would assume the role of Executive Vice-President and Chief Operating Officer, following the retirement of Jim Vena, effective July&nbsp;1, 2016.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;PUNCTUATION-WRAP:SIMPLE;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Strategic Initiatives and Capital Spending
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	CN&#146;s business strategy is anchored on the continuous pursuit of
<I>
	Operational and Service Excellence
</I>
	, an unwavering commitment to safety and sustainability, and the development of a solid team of motivated and competent railroaders. CN&#146;s success and long-term economic viability depends on the presence of a supportive regulatory and policy environment that drives investment and innovation. CN&#146;s success also depends on a stream of capital investments that supports its business strategy. These investments cover a wide range of areas, from track infrastructure and rolling stock, to information and operating technologies, and other equipment and assets that improve the safety, efficiency and reliability of CN&#146;s service offering. Investments in track infrastructure enhance the productivity and integrity of the plant, and increase the capacity and the fluidity of the network. The acquisition of new locomotives and railcars generates several key benefits. New locomotives increase fuel productivity and efficiency, and improve the reliability of service. Locomotives equipped with distributed power allow for greater productivity of trains, particularly in cold weather, while improving train handling and safety. Targeted railcar acquisitions aim to tap growth opportunities, complementing the fleet of privately owned railcars that traverse CN&#146;s network. CN&#146;s strategic investments in information technology provide access to timely and accurate information which supports CN&#146;s ongoing efforts to drive innovation and efficiency in service, cost control, asset utilization, safety and employee engagement.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	CN is committed to the safety of its employees, the communities in which it operates and the environment. Safety consciousness permeates every aspect of CN&#146;s operations. The Company&#146;s long-term safety improvement is driven by continued significant investments in infrastructure, rigorous safety processes and a focus on employee training and safety awareness. CN continues to strengthen its safety culture by investing significantly in training, coaching, recognition and employee involvement initiatives.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	CN spent $2.75 billion in its capital program, with $1.6 billion invested to maintain the safety and integrity of the network, particularly track infrastructure; $0.55 billion for equipment capital expenditures, including 90 new high-horsepower locomotives, $0.3 billion on initiatives to support growth and drive productivity, and $0.3 billion for the U.S. federal government legislative Positive Train Control (PTC) implementation.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>

<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Acquisitions and Dispositions
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On December&nbsp;1, 2016, the Company completed the sale of approximately one mile of elevated track leading into Montreal&#146;s Central Station, together with the rail fixtures, to CDPQ Infra Inc., a wholly owned subsidiary of the Caisse de d&#233;p&#244;t et placement du Qu&#233;bec, for cash proceeds of $85 million before transaction costs. The transaction resulted in a gain on disposal of $76 million ($66 million after-tax) that was recorded in Other income under the full accrual method of accounting for real estate transactions.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Financial Management Initiatives
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On January&nbsp;5, 2016, CN filed a new shelf prospectus with the Canadian securities regulators and a registration statement with the U.S. Securities and Exchange Commission (SEC) pursuant to which CN may issue up to $6.0 billion of debt securities in the Canadian and U.S. markets.&#160; The shelf prospectus and registration statement expire on February&nbsp;4, 2018 and replace CN&#146;s previous shelf prospectus and registration statement.&#160; Access to capital markets under the shelf prospectus and registration statement is dependent on market conditions at the time of pricing.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="BORDER:NONE;FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="BORDER:NONE;FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has a commercial paper program in Canada and in the U.S. Both programs are backstopped by the Company&#146;s revolving credit facility, enabling it to issue commercial paper up to a maximum aggregate principal amount of $1.3 billion, or the U.S. dollar equivalent, on a combined basis, which was increased from $800 million, effective May&nbsp;5, 2016.
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="BORDER:NONE;">
	&#160;A
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="BORDER:NONE;">
	s at December&nbsp;31, 2016, the Company had total commercial paper borrowings of $605 million (U.S. $451 million). The commercial paper programs, which are subject to market rates in effect at the time of financing, provide the Company with a flexible financing alternative at a low cost, and can be used for general corporate purposes. The weighted-average interest rate on these borrowings was 0.65%.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has an agreement to sell an undivided co-ownership interest in a revolving pool of accounts receivable to unrelated trusts for maximum cash proceeds of $450 million. On October&nbsp;25, 2016, the Company extended the term of its agreement by one year to February&nbsp;1, 2019.&#160; As at December&nbsp;31, 2016, the Company had no proceeds received under the accounts receivable securitization program. The accounts receivable securitization program provides the Company with readily available short-term financing for general corporate use.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has an unsecured revolving credit facility with a consortium of lenders. On March&nbsp;11, 2016, the credit facility agreement was amended, which increased the credit facility from $800 million to $1.3 billion, effective May&nbsp;5, 2016, consisting of a tranche for $420 million maturing on May&nbsp;5, 2019 and a tranche for $880 million maturing on May&nbsp;5, 2021. The increased capacity provides the Company with additional financial flexibility. The credit facility agreement allows for an increase in the credit facility amount, up to a maximum of $1.8 billion, as well as the option to extend the term by an additional year at each anniversary date, subject to the consent of individual lenders. The credit facility provides for borrowings at various interest rates, including the Canadian prime rate, bankers&#146; acceptance rates, the U.S. federal funds effective rate and the London Interbank Offered Rate (LIBOR), plus applicable margins, based on CN&#146;s debt credit ratings.&#160; The credit facility is available for working capital and general corporate purposes, including backstopping the Company&#146;s commercial paper programs. The credit facility agreement has one financial covenant, which limits debt as a percentage of total capitalization, and with which the Company is in compliance. As at December&nbsp;31, 2016, the Company had no outstanding borrowings under its revolving credit facility and there were no draws during the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2016.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has a series of committed bilateral letter of credit facility agreements. During 2016, the Company extended the expiry date of the majority of these agreements by one year to April&nbsp;28, 2019, and entered into various uncommitted bilateral letter of credit facility agreements. These agreements are held with various banks to support the Company&#146;s requirements to post letters of credit in the ordinary course of business. Under these agreements, the Company has the option from time to time to pledge collateral in the form of cash or cash equivalents, for a minimum term of one month, equal to at least the face value of the letters of credit issued. As at December&nbsp;31, 2016, the
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="4" COLOR="RED" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:RED;FONT-SIZE:13.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	2016 Annual Information Form

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	Company had outstanding letters of credit of $451 million under the committed facilities from a total available amount of $508 million and $68 million under the uncommitted facilities. As at December&nbsp;31, 2016, included in Restricted cash and cash equivalents was $426 million and $68 million which were pledged as collateral under the committed and uncommitted bilateral letter of credit facilities, respectively.

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On August&nbsp;2, 2016, under its shelf prospectus and registration statement, the Company issued US$650 million ($848 million) 3.20% Notes due 2046 in the U.S. capital markets, which resulted in net proceeds of $832 million and on February&nbsp;23, 2016, under its shelf prospectus and registration statement, the Company issued US$500 million ($686 million) 2.75% Notes due 2026 in the U.S. capital markets, which resulted in net proceeds of $677 million. The proceeds from both debt issuances were used for general corporate purposes, including the redemption and refinancing of outstanding indebtedness, and share repurchases.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On October&nbsp;25, 2016, the Board of Directors approved a new share repurchase program which allows for the repurchase of up to 33.0 million Common Shares, between October&nbsp;30, 2016 and October&nbsp;29, 2017, pursuant to a normal course issuer bid at prevailing market prices plus brokerage fees, or such other prices as may be permitted by the TSX. On November&nbsp;2, 2016 and on December&nbsp;13, 2016, the Company announced that it entered into agreements with third parties to repurchase Common Shares through daily purchases subject to a maximum of 2,723,662 Common Shares and 4,840,000 Common Shares, respectively.&#160; Purchases pursuant to the agreements took place from November&nbsp;7, 2016 to December&nbsp;30, 2016 and will be completed by March&nbsp;15, 2017. Pursuant to the terms of the agreements, and subject to the terms of issuer bid exemption orders issued by the Ontario Securities Commission (&#147;OSC&#148;), the third parties purchased CN&#146;s Common Shares on the open market for their own account in accordance with the rules&nbsp;applicable to the normal course issuer bid, for the purpose of ultimately fulfilling their delivery obligations to CN under the agreements. The price that CN paid for Common Shares purchased by it from the third parties under the agreements was negotiated by CN and the third parties and was at a discount to the prevailing market price of CN&#146;s Common Shares on the TSX at the time of the purchase.&#160; The purchases formed part of CN&#146;s repurchase of up to 33.0 million Common Shares under its October&nbsp;25, 2016 share repurchase program.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On February&nbsp;5, February&nbsp;19, March&nbsp;16 and July&nbsp;29, 2016, the Company announced that it entered into agreements with third parties to repurchase Common Shares through daily purchases subject to an aggregate maximum of 21.895 million Common Shares.&#160; The purchases took place from February&nbsp;12, 2016 to October&nbsp;29, 2016. Pursuant to the terms of the agreements, and subject to the terms of issuer bid exemption orders issued by the OSC, the third parties purchased CN&#146;s Common Shares on the open market for their own account in accordance with the rules&nbsp;applicable to the normal course issuer bid, for the purpose of ultimately fulfilling their delivery obligations to CN under the agreements. The price that CN paid for Common Shares purchased by it from the third parties under the agreements was negotiated by CN and the third parties and was at a discount to the prevailing market price of CN&#146;s Common Shares on the TSX at the time of the purchase.&#160; All the purchases formed part of CN&#146;s then current share repurchase program.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On March&nbsp;23, 2016, the Company served notice to commence bargaining for the renewal of the collective agreements with the Teamsters Canada Rail Conference (TCRC) governing approximately 2,500 train conductors and yard coordinators, which expired on July&nbsp;22, 2016. On June&nbsp;29, 2016, the Company filed a notice of dispute seeking conciliation assistance. On July&nbsp;14, 2016, the Minister of Labour appointed two conciliation officers to assist the parties with their negotiations. On September&nbsp;16, 2016, the Company and the TCRC agreed to extend the conciliation period on a voluntary basis.

	On October&nbsp;12, 2016, the Company served notice to commence bargaining for the renewal of the collective agreement with the International Brotherhood of Electrical Workers (IBEW) governing approximately 700 signals and

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="4" COLOR="RED" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:RED;FONT-SIZE:13.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	2016 Annual Information Form
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	communications workers, which expired on December&nbsp;31, 2016. On December&nbsp;15, 2016, CN filed a notice of dispute seeking conciliation assistance with the Minister of Labour. On December&nbsp;29, 2016, the Minister of Labour appointed two conciliation officers to assist the parties in their efforts to renew the collective agreement.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	Under the Canada Labour Code, the law governing labor relations for the Canadian railroad industry, collective agreements remain in force until such time as the parties have either reached a renewed agreement or the dispute resolution mechanisms in the Code have been exhausted.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	U.S. workforce
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	As of February&nbsp;1, 2017, the Company had in place agreements with bargaining units representing the entire unionized workforce at Grand Trunk Western Railroad Company (GTW), companies owned by Illinois Central Corporation (ICC), companies owned by Wisconsin Central Ltd. (WC), Bessemer&nbsp;&amp; Lake Erie Railroad Company (BLE) and The Pittsburgh and Conneaut Dock Company (PCD). Agreements in place have various moratorium provisions up to 2018, which preserve the status quo in respect of the given collective agreement during the terms of such moratoriums. All collective agreements covering non-operating craft employees and six collective agreements covering roughly half of the operating craft population of 3,000 employees are currently under renegotiation.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	During 2016, the Company renewed four collective agreements with the United Transportation Union (a division of the International Association of Sheet Metal, Air, Rail, and Transportation Workers - SMART) governing 65 yardmasters at GTW, two WC bargaining units and a small subset working on the ICC.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The general approach to labor negotiations by U.S. Class&nbsp;I railroads is to bargain on a collective national basis with the industry, which GTW,&nbsp;ICC, WC and BLE have agreed to participate in, for collective agreements covering non-operating employees. Collective agreements covering operating employees at GTW,&nbsp;ICC, WC, BLE and all employees at PCD continue to be bargained on a local (corporate) basis.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	Where negotiations are ongoing, the terms and conditions of existing agreements generally continue to apply until new agreements are reached or the processes of the
<I>
	Railway Labor Act
</I>
	have been exhausted
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<B>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	2015 Highlights
</FONT>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;PUNCTUATION-WRAP:SIMPLE;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Strategic Initiatives and Capital Spending
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	In 2015, CN spent $2.7 billion in its capital program, with $1.53 billion targeted at maintaining the safety and integrity of the network, particularly track infrastructure.&#160; This investment included the replacement of rail, ties, and other track materials, bridge improvements, as well as various branch line upgrades. CN invested significantly to build for the future, increasing network capacity, resilience and fluidity across its network, including its Edmonton-Winnipeg and Winnipeg-Chicago corridors. As part of its overall capital program, CN invested more than $120 million in 2015 to install sections of double tracks, extended sidings, crossovers and yard improvements on main lines in the two corridors.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	In 2015, CN&#146;s equipment capital expenditures reached $555 million, allowing the Company to be ready for growth opportunities and to improve the quality of the fleet, including the acquisition of 90 new high-horsepower locomotives. Orders have been placed for 90 additional new locomotives which were delivered in 2016. CN also spent $615 million on initiatives to support growth and drive productivity, such as transloads and distribution centers; and information technology to improve service and operating efficiency.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company strengthened its commitment to
<I>
	Operational and Service Excellence
</I>
	through a wide range of innovations anchored on its continuous improvement philosophy. CN built on its industry leadership in terms of fast and reliable hub-to-hub service by continuing to improve across the range of customer touch points. The Company&#146;s
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="4" COLOR="RED" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:RED;FONT-SIZE:13.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	2016 Annual Information Form
</FONT>
</I>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	major push in first-mile/last-mile service is all about improving the quality of customer interactions &#150; developing a sharper outside-in perspective; better monitoring of traffic forecasts; higher and more responsive car order fulfillment; and proactive customer communication at the local level, supported by iAdvise, an information tool that is improving the reliability and consistency of shipment information.
</FONT>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Financial Management Initiatives
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="BORDER:NONE;FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="BORDER:NONE;FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company established a commercial paper program in the U.S. during the second quarter of 2015 in addition to its existing commercial paper program in Canada. Both programs are backstopped by the Company&#146;s revolving credit facility, enabling it to issue commercial paper up to a maximum aggregate principal amount of $800 million, or the U.S. dollar equivalent, on a combined basis.
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="BORDER:NONE;">
	&#160; A
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="BORDER:NONE;">
	s at December&nbsp;31, 2015, the Company had total commercial paper borrowings of $458 million (U.S. $331 million).&#160; The weighted-average interest rate on these borrowings was 0.41%.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has an agreement to sell an undivided co-ownership interest in a revolving pool of accounts receivable to unrelated trusts for maximum cash proceeds of $450 million. On June&nbsp;18, 2015, the expiry date of the agreement was extended by one year to February&nbsp;1, 2018. As at December&nbsp;31, 2015, the Company had no proceeds received under the accounts receivable securitization program. The accounts receivable securitization program provides the Company with readily available short-term financing for general corporate use.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has an $800 million revolving credit facility agreement with a consortium of lenders.&#160; The agreement, which contains customary terms and conditions, allows for an increase in the facility amount, up to a maximum of $1.3 billion, as well as the option to extend the term by an additional year at each anniversary date, subject to the consent of individual lenders.&#160; The Company exercised such option, and on March&nbsp;12, 2015, the expiry date of the agreement was extended by one year to May&nbsp;5, 2020.&#160; The credit facility is available for general corporate purposes, including back-stopping the Company&#146;s commercial paper program, and provides for borrowings at various interest rates, including the Canadian prime rate, bankers&#146; acceptance rates, the U.S. federal funds effective rate and the London Interbank Offered Rate (LIBOR), plus applicable margins.&#160; The credit facility agreement has one financial covenant, which limits debt as a percentage of total capitalization, and with which the Company is in compliance.&#160; As at December&nbsp;31, 2015, the Company had no outstanding borrowings under its revolving credit facility and there were no draws during the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2015.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has a series of bilateral letter of credit facility agreements with various banks to support its requirements to post letters of credit in the ordinary course of business.&#160; On March&nbsp;12, 2015 the expiry date of these agreements was extended by one year to April&nbsp;28, 2018.&#160; Under these agreements, the Company has the option from time to time to pledge collateral in the form of cash or cash equivalents, for a minimum term of one month, equal to at least the face value of the letters of credit issued
<B>
	.
</B>
	&#160;As at December&nbsp;31, 2015, the Company had letters of credit drawn of $551 million from a total committed amount of $575 million by the various banks.&#160; As at December&nbsp;31, 2015, cash and cash equivalents of $523 million were pledged as collateral and recorded as Restricted cash and cash equivalents on the Consolidated Balance Sheet.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On September&nbsp;11, 2015, CN announced that the TSX had accepted CN&#146;s amended 2014-2015 notice of intention of October&nbsp;2014 to make a normal course issuer bid. The notice was amended to permit the repurchase by CN of its Common Shares under a specific share repurchase program during the term of the Normal Course Issuer Bid. The purchases formed part of CN&#146;s 2014-2015 Normal Course Issuer Bid for up to 28.0 million Common Shares announced on October&nbsp;21, 2014. CN entered into an agreement with a third party to repurchase its Common Shares through daily purchases that took place from September&nbsp;16 to October&nbsp;23, 2015. Pursuant to the terms of the agreement, and subject to the terms of an issuer bid exemption order issued by the OSC, the third party purchased CN&#146;s Common Shares on the open market for its own account in accordance with the rules&nbsp;applicable to the normal course issuer bid, for the purpose of ultimately fulfilling its delivery obligations to CN under the agreement. The price that CN paid for Common Shares purchased by it from the third party under the agreement was negotiated by CN
</FONT>
</P>

<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;

	2016 Annual Information Form
</FONT>
</I>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	and the third party and was at a discount to the prevailing market price of CN&#146;s Common Shares on the TSX at the time of the purchase.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On September&nbsp;22, 2015, under its then current shelf prospectus and registration statement, the Company issued $350 million 2.80% Notes due 2025,
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	$400 million 3.95% Notes due 2045 and $100 million 4.00% Notes due 2065,
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	in the Canadian capital markets, which resulted in total net proceeds of $841 million, intended for general corporate purposes, including the redemption and refinancing of outstanding indebtedness and share repurchases.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On October&nbsp;27, 2015, the Board of Directors approved a new share repurchase program which allowed for the repurchase of up to 33.0 million Common Shares, between October&nbsp;30, 2015 and October&nbsp;29, 2016, pursuant to a normal course issuer bid at prevailing market prices plus brokerage fees, or such other prices as may be permitted by the TSX and on the same day, the Company announced that it would enter into an agreement with a third party to repurchase Common Shares through daily purchases subject to a maximum of 4.0 million Common Shares.&#160; The agreement was amended on November&nbsp;30, 2015 to increase the number of Common Shares to be purchased to 5.175 million Common Shares. The purchases took place from October&nbsp;30, 2015 to December&nbsp;24, 2015. Pursuant to the terms of the agreement, and subject to the terms of an issuer bid exemption order issued by the OSC, the third party purchased CN&#146;s Common Shares on the open market for its own account in accordance with the rules&nbsp;applicable to the Normal Course Issuer Bid, for the purpose of ultimately fulfilling its delivery obligations to CN under the agreement. The price that CN paid for Common Shares purchased by it from the third party under the agreement was negotiated by CN and the third party and was at a discount to the prevailing market price of CN&#146;s Common Shares on the TSX at the time of the purchase.&#160; The purchases formed part of CN&#146;s repurchase of up to 33.0 million Common Shares under its share repurchase program.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On December&nbsp;18, 2015, the Company announced that it had entered into an agreement with a third party to repurchase Common Shares through daily purchases subject to a maximum of 4.356 million Common Shares.&#160; The purchases took place from December&nbsp;29, 2015 to February&nbsp;29, 2016. Pursuant to the terms of the agreement, and subject to the terms of an issuer bid exemption order issued by the OSC, the third party purchased CN&#146;s Common Shares on the open market for its own account in accordance with the rules&nbsp;applicable to the normal course issuer bid, for the purpose of ultimately fulfilling its delivery obligations to CN under the agreement. The price that CN paid for Common Shares purchased by it from the third party under the agreement was negotiated by CN and the third party and was at a discount to the prevailing market price of CN&#146;s Common Shares on the TSX at the time of the purchase.&#160; The purchases formed part of CN&#146;s repurchase of up to 33.0 million Common Shares under its share repurchase program.
</FONT>
</P>

<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">

<FONT SIZE="2" COLOR="BLACK" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:BLACK;FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On January&nbsp;30, 2015, the agreement for the renewal of the collective agreement with the United Steelworkers of America (USW) governing maintenance of way employees was ratified. The new collective agreement expires on December&nbsp;31, 2018.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">

</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	for the renewal of the collective agreement with the
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	Teamsters Canada Rail Conference (TCRC-RCTC) governing rail traffic controllers was ratified. The new collective agreement expires on December&nbsp;31, 2018.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">

<P STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">

	On March&nbsp;13, 2015, the agreements
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	for the renewal of the collective agreements with
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	Unifor governing clerical, intermodal employees and owner operator truck drivers were ratified. The new collective agreements expire on March&nbsp;31, 2019.

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="4" COLOR="RED" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:RED;FONT-SIZE:13.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	2016 Annual Information Form
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On March&nbsp;17, 2015, the agreement
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	for the renewal of the collective agreement with
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	Unifor governing shopcraft employees was ratified. The new collective agreement expires on December&nbsp;31, 2018.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On April&nbsp;16, 2015, the agreement
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	for the renewal of the collective agreement with
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	the TCRC governing locomotive engineers (TCRC-LE) was ratified. The new collective agreement expires on December&nbsp;31, 2017.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	Under the Canada Labour Code, the law governing labor relations for the Canadian railroad industry, collective agreements remain in force until such time as the parties have either reached a renewed agreement or the dispute resolution mechanisms in the Code have been exhausted.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	U.S. workforce
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	As of February&nbsp;1, 2016, the Company had in place agreements with bargaining units representing the entire unionized workforce at Grand Trunk Western Railroad Company (GTW), companies owned by Illinois Central Corporation (ICC), companies owned by Wisconsin Central Ltd. (WC), Bessemer&nbsp;&amp; Lake Erie Railroad Company (BLE) and The Pittsburgh and Conneaut Dock Company (PCD). Agreements in place have various moratorium provisions up to 2018, which preserve the status quo in respect of the given collective agreement during the terms of such moratoriums. All collective agreements covering non-operating craft employees and four collective agreements covering operating craft employees are currently under renegotiation.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	During 2015, the Company renewed a collective agreement with the United Transportation Union (UTU) (a division of the International Association of Sheet Metal, Air, Rail, and Transportation Workers - SMART) governing conductors on the Grand Trunk Western. On January&nbsp;15, 2016, the Company renewed three additional collective agreements with UTU, governing 57 yardmasters at GTW, WC, and a small subset working on the ICC.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The general approach to labor negotiations by U.S. Class&nbsp;I railroads is to bargain on a collective national basis with the industry, which GTW,&nbsp;ICC, WC and BLE have agreed to participate in, effective January&nbsp;2015, for collective agreements covering non-operating employees. Collective agreements covering operating employees at GTW,&nbsp;ICC, WC, BLE and all employees at PCD continue to be bargained on a local (corporate) basis.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	Where negotiations are ongoing, the terms and conditions of existing agreements generally continue to apply until new agreements are reached or the processes of the
<I>
	Railway Labor Act
</I>
	have been exhausted.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<B>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	2014 Highlights
</FONT>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Acquisitions and Dispositions
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On February&nbsp;28, 2014, the Company closed a transaction with Agence M&#233;tropolitaine de Transport to sell the Deux-Montagnes subdivision between Saint-Eustache and Montreal, Quebec, including the Mont-Royal tunnel, together with the rail fixtures (collectively Deux-Montagnes), for cash proceeds of $97 million before transaction costs.&#160; Under the agreement, the Company obtained the perpetual right to operate freight trains over the Deux-Montagnes at its then current level of operating activity, with the possibility of increasing its operating activity for additional consideration.&#160; The transaction resulted in a gain on disposal of $80 million ($72 million after-tax) that was recorded in Other income under the full accrual method of accounting for real estate transactions.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On September&nbsp;4, 2014, the Company closed a transaction with Metrolinx to sell a segment of the Guelph subdivision located between Georgetown and Kitchener, Ontario, together with the rail fixtures and certain passenger agreements (collectively the Guelph), for cash proceeds of $76 million before transaction costs.&#160; The Company did not meet all the conditions to record the sale under the full accrual method for real estate transactions as it continues to have substantial continuing involvement on the Guelph.&#160; The Company will have relinquished substantially all of
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="4" COLOR="RED" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:RED;FONT-SIZE:13.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	2016 Annual Information Form

<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	the risks and rewards of ownership on the Guelph in 2018, at which time the gain on the sale is expected to be recognized.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Strategic Initiatives and Capital Spending
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	In 2014, CN spent approximately $2.3 billion in its capital program, with $1.25 billion targeted at maintaining the safety and integrity of the network.&#160; This investment included the replacement of rail, ties, and other track materials, bridge improvements, as well as various branch line upgrades. CN invested significantly to build for the future, increasing network capacity, resilience and fluidity across its network, including its Edmonton-Winnipeg and Winnipeg-Chicago corridors. As part of its overall capital program, CN invested more than $100 million in 2014 to install sections of double tracks, extended sidings, crossovers, high-speed switches and yard improvements on main lines in the two corridors.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	In 2014, CN&#146;s equipment capital expenditures reached approximately $375 million, allowing the Company to tap growth opportunities and improve the quality of the fleet. In order to handle the expected traffic increase and improve operational efficiency, 60 new high-horsepower locomotives were added to the fleet in 2014. Furthermore, orders were placed for 180 additional new locomotives: 90 delivered in 2015 and 90 delivered in 2016. CN also spent approximately $575 million on initiatives to support growth and drive productivity, such as transloads and distribution centers; and information technology to improve service and operating efficiency.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	As part of its objective to build a solid team of railroaders, the Company opened two new state-of-the-art training facilities in 2014, in Winnipeg, Manitoba and Homewood,&nbsp;Illinois, at a cost of $55 million, aimed at preparing employees to be highly skilled, safety conscious and confident in their work environment. Curricula for technical training and leadership development was also improved to meet the learning needs of CN
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	&#146;
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	s railroaders &#150; both current and future. These programs and initiatives provided a solid platform for the assessment and development of the Company
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	&#146;
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	s talent
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	pool, and are tightly integrated with the Company
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	&#146;
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	s business strategy.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;PUNCTUATION-WRAP:SIMPLE;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company also strengthened its commitment to
<I>
	Operational and Service Excellence
</I>
	through a wide range of innovations anchored on its continuous improvement philosophy. Through a portfolio of initiatives called CustomerFIRST, the Company innovated to address key customer pinch points, including the
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	first-mile and last-mile of the shipment cycle. iAdvise, an information tool that is improving the reliability and consistency of shipment information, was the latest initiative in CN&#146;s strategy to communicate better with customers.&#160; In 2014, CN rolled out its iAdvise tool to a significant number of its largest customers.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;">
	Financial Management Initiatives
</FONT>
</I>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has a commercial paper program, which is back-stopped by its revolving credit facility, enabling it to issue commercial paper up to a maximum aggregate principal amount of $800 million, or the U.S. dollar equivalent. As at December&nbsp;31, 2014, the Company had no commercial paper borrowings.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has an agreement to sell an undivided co-ownership interest in a revolving pool of accounts receivable to unrelated trusts for maximum cash proceeds of $450 million. On July&nbsp;23, 2014, the expiry date of the agreement was extended by one year to February&nbsp;1, 2017.&#160; As such, as at December&nbsp;31, 2014, the Company recorded $50 million of proceeds received under the accounts receivable securitization program in the Current portion of long-term debt on the Consolidated Balance Sheet at a weighted-average interest rate of 1.24% which is secured by and limited to $56 million of accounts receivable.&#160; The accounts receivable securitization program provides the Company with readily available short-term financing for general corporate use.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has an $800 million revolving credit facility agreement with a consortium of lenders.&#160; The agreement, which contains customary terms and conditions, allows for an increase in the facility amount, up to a maximum of $1.3 billion, as well as the option to extend the term by an additional year at each anniversary date, subject to the
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>

<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	consent of individual lenders.&#160; The Company exercised such option and on March&nbsp;14, 2014, the expiry date of the agreement was extended by one year to May&nbsp;5, 2019.&#160; The credit facility is available for general corporate purposes, including back-stopping the Company&#146;s commercial paper program, and provides for borrowings at various interest rates, including the Canadian prime rate, bankers&#146; acceptance rates, the U.S. federal funds effective rate and the LIBOR, plus applicable margins.&#160; The credit facility agreement has one financial covenant, which limits debt as a percentage of total capitalization, and with which the Company is in compliance.&#160; As at December&nbsp;31, 2014, the Company had no outstanding borrowings under its revolving credit facility and there were no draws during the year ended December&nbsp;31, 2014.

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company has a series of bilateral letter of credit facility agreements with various banks to support its requirements to post letters of credit in the ordinary course of business.&#160; On March&nbsp;14, 2014, the expiry date of these agreements was extended by one year to April&nbsp;28, 2017.&#160; Under these agreements, the Company has the option from time to time to pledge collateral in the form of cash or cash equivalents, for a minimum term of one month, equal to at least the face value of the letters of credit issued.&#160; As at December&nbsp;31, 2014, the Company had letters of credit drawn of $487 million from a total committed amount of $511 million by the various banks.&#160; As at December&nbsp;31, 2014, cash and cash equivalents of $463 million were pledged as collateral and recorded as Restricted cash and cash equivalents on the Consolidated Balance Sheet.

<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On October&nbsp;21, 2014, the Board of Directors approved a new share repurchase program which allowed for the repurchase of up to 28.0 million Common Shares, between October&nbsp;24, 2014 and October&nbsp;23, 2015, pursuant to a normal course issuer bid at prevailing market prices plus brokerage fees, or such other prices as may be permitted by the TSX.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On October&nbsp;27, 2014, the Company announced its intention to repurchase up to 5.175 million of its Common Shares from an arm&#146;s-length third-party seller by means of private agreements formalized at the time of each such purchase.&#160; Such repurchases were made pursuant and subject to the terms of an issuer bid exemption order issued by the OSC.&#160; The purchases formed part of CN&#146;s repurchase of up to 28.0 million Common Shares under the share repurchase program announced on October&nbsp;21, 2014.&#160; The price that CN paid for any Common Shares purchased under such private agreements was negotiated by CN and the third-party seller and was at a discount to the prevailing market price of CN&#146;s Common Shares on the TSX at the time of the purchase.
</FONT>
</P>

<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	On November&nbsp;14, 2014, under its then current shelf prospectus and registration statement, the Company completed a two-tranche debt offering of U.S.$600 million ($682 million), comprised of U.S.$250 million ($284 million) Floating Rate Notes due 2017, and U.S.$350 million ($398 million) 2.95% Notes due 2024 in the U.S. capital markets, which resulted in net proceeds of U.S.$593 million ($675 million), intended for general corporate purposes, including the redemption and refinancing of outstanding indebtedness, and share repurchases.

<B>
<FONT SIZE="2" COLOR="BLACK" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:BLACK;FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	ITEM 4
</FONT>
</B>
<FONT SIZE="1" COLOR="BLACK" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:BLACK;FONT-SIZE:3.0PT;">
	&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;
</FONT>
<B>
<FONT COLOR="BLACK" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:BLACK;FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	DESCRIPTION OF THE BUSINESS
</FONT>
</B>
<A NAME="A17-3171_140F_HTM_ITEM4DESCRIPTIONOFTHEBUSINESS_125647">
</A>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT .5IN;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;TEXT-INDENT:-.5IN;">
<B>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	4.1
</FONT>
</B>
<FONT SIZE="1" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:3.0PT;">
	&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;
</FONT>
<B>
<I>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	O
</FONT>
</I>
</B>
<B>
<I>
<FONT SIZE="1" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:8.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	VERVIEW
</FONT>
</I>
</B>
<A NAME="A17-3171_140F_HTM_A4_1OVERVIEW_125648">
</A>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	CN is engaged in the rail and related transportation business. CN&#146;s network of approximately 20,000 route miles of track spans Canada and mid-America, uniquely connecting three coasts: the Atlantic, the Pacific and the Gulf of Mexico and serving the cities and ports of Vancouver, Prince Rupert (British Columbia), Montreal, Halifax, New Orleans, and Mobile (Alabama), and the metropolitan areas of Toronto, Edmonton, Winnipeg, Calgary, Chicago, Memphis, Detroit, Duluth (Minnesota)/Superior (Wisconsin), and Jackson (Mississippi), with connections to all points in North America. CN&#146;s extensive network and efficient connections to all Class&nbsp;I railroads provide CN customers access to all three North American Free Trade Agreement (NAFTA) nations.&#160; CN handles over $250 billion worth of goods annually and carries almost 300 million tons of cargo, serving exporters, importers, retailers, farmers and manufacturers.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	CN&#146;s freight revenues are derived from seven commodity groups representing a diversified and balanced portfolio of goods transported between a wide range of origins and destinations. This product and geographic diversity better positions the Company to face economic fluctuations and enhances its potential for growth opportunities. In 2016, no individual commodity group accounted for more than 24% of total revenues. From a geographic standpoint, 17% of revenues relate to U.S. domestic traffic, 34% transborder traffic, 18% Canadian domestic traffic and 31% overseas traffic. The Company is the originating carrier for approximately 85% of traffic moving along its network, which allows it both to capitalize on service advantages and build on opportunities to efficiently use assets.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	Revenues generated by the Company during the year are influenced by seasonal weather conditions, general economic conditions, cyclical demand for rail transportation, and competitive forces in the transportation marketplace. Operating expenses reflect the impact of freight volumes, seasonal weather conditions, labor costs, fuel prices, and the Company&#146;s productivity initiatives.
</FONT>
</P>

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;

<P STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" COLOR="BLACK" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="COLOR:BLACK;FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	In addition to its Employment Equity Policy (for Canadian employees) and Equal Employment Opportunity Policy (for U.S. employees), CN maintains a comprehensive Human Rights Policy and a Harassment Free Environment Policy for its Canadian employees
</FONT>
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	and a Prohibited Harassment, Discrimination and Anti-Retaliation Policy for its U.S. employees.
<FONT COLOR="BLACK" STYLE="COLOR:BLACK;">
	&#160;These policies affirm CN&#146;s commitment to ensuring that there is no discrimination against any employee or applicant based on grounds of religion, race, sex, nationality, disability or any other prohibited grounds of discrimination.&#160; The policy extends to recruitment, selection and compensation practices, as well as to working conditions and the work environment.&#160; All Company vice-presidents have been mandated with the responsibility of implementing these policies and ensuring that all work practices are in compliance.&#160; Internal complaint procedures have been established whereby any person covered by the Harassment Free Environment Policy and the Employment Equity Policy (for Canadian employees) or the Equal Employment Opportunity Policy and
</FONT>
	Prohibited Harassment, Discrimination and Anti-Retaliation Policy
<FONT COLOR="BLACK" STYLE="COLOR:BLACK;">
	(for U.S. employees) can contact his or her human resources director or human resources manager who will address his or her complaint.&#160; The employee can also call either the Human Resources Center, which will forward the complaint to the appropriate human resources manager for further handling, or the CN Ombudsman directly, who can be contacted on a confidential basis.
</FONT>
	As part of CN&#146;s commitment to providing a safe, healthy and violence-free workplace for all employees, CN has in place a Workplace Violence Prevention Policy which applies to all employees
<I>
	.
</I>
	&#160;The objective of this policy is to reiterate the prohibition of workplace violence at CN and set out how threats, acts or risks of workplace violence are to be reported and addressed.
</FONT>

	&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;

<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company&#146;s operations are subject to regulations both in Canada and in the U.S.&#160; A summary of such regulations is provided below.&#160; For a complete discussion of recent and pending legislative and other regulatory developments both in Canada and in the U.S., see the section entitled &#147;Regulation&#148; in the Business risks discussion located on pages&nbsp;43 to 48 of the MD&amp;A, which are incorporated by reference herein.
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;PUNCTUATION-WRAP:SIMPLE;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<B>
<I>
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;FONT-STYLE:ITALIC;FONT-WEIGHT:BOLD;">
	Economic regulation &#150; Canada
</FONT>
</I>
</B>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;PUNCTUATION-WRAP:SIMPLE;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	The Company&#146;s rail operations in Canada are subject to economic regulation by the Canadian Transportation Agency (Agency) under the
<I>
	Canada Transportation Act
</I>
	(CTA). The CTA provides rate and service remedies, including final
</FONT>
</P>
<P STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;PUNCTUATION-WRAP:SIMPLE;TEXT-ALIGN:JUSTIFY;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
<DIV STYLE="BORDER:NONE;BORDER-BOTTOM:SOLID WINDOWTEXT 1.0PT;PADDING:0IN 0IN 1.0PT 0IN;">
<P ALIGN="RIGHT" STYLE="BORDER:NONE;FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;PADDING:0IN;TEXT-ALIGN:RIGHT;">
<FONT FACE="ARIAL">
	13
</FONT>
<A NAME="A17-3171_140F_HTM_PB_13_123516_2075">
</A>
</P>
</DIV>
<P ALIGN="CENTER" STYLE="MARGIN:0IN 0IN .0001PT;TEXT-ALIGN:CENTER;">
<FONT SIZE="2" FACE="ARIAL" STYLE="FONT-SIZE:10.0PT;">
	&nbsp;
</FONT>
</P>
